     <p>
      <b>
       HDMI
      </b>
      (
      <b>
       High-Definition Multimedia Interface
      </b>
      ) is a
      <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_hardware" title="Proprietary hardware">
       proprietary
      </a>
      audio/video interface for transferring
      <a href="/wiki/Uncompressed_video" title="Uncompressed video">
       uncompressed video
      </a>
      data and compressed or uncompressed
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio" title="Digital audio">
       digital audio
      </a>
      data from an HDMI-compliant source device, such as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Display_controller" title="Display controller">
       display controller
      </a>
      , to a compatible
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_display_unit" title="Visual display unit">
       computer monitor
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Video_projector" title="Video projector">
       video projector
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">
       digital television
      </a>
      , or
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio" title="Digital audio">
       digital audio
      </a>
      device.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIFAQ_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIFAQ-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI is a digital replacement for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Analog_video" title="Analog video">
       analog video
      </a>
      standards.
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI implements the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEA-861" title="CEA-861">
       EIA/CEA-861
      </a>
      standards, which define video formats and waveforms, transport of compressed, uncompressed, and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_pulse-code_modulation" title="Linear pulse-code modulation">
       LPCM
      </a>
      audio, auxiliary data, and implementations of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extended_display_identification_data" title="Extended display identification data">
       VESA EDID
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      CEA-861 signals carried by HDMI are electrically compatible with the CEA-861 signals used by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_visual_interface" title="Digital visual interface">
       digital visual interface
      </a>
      (DVI). No signal conversion is necessary, nor is there a loss of video quality when a DVI-to-HDMI adapter is used.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsAppC_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsAppC-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="#CEC">
       CEC
      </a>
      (Consumer Electronics Control) capability allows HDMI devices to control each other when necessary and allows the user to operate multiple devices with one
      <a href="/wiki/Remote_control" title="Remote control">
       remote control
      </a>
      handset.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs6.3_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs6.3-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Several versions of HDMI have been developed and deployed since initial release of the technology but all use the same cable and connector. Other than improved audio and video capacity, performance, resolution and color spaces, newer versions have optional advanced features such as
      <a href="/wiki/3D_television" title="3D television">
       3D
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ethernet" title="Ethernet">
       Ethernet
      </a>
      data connection, and
      <a href="/wiki/HDMI#CEC" title="HDMI">
       CEC (Consumer Electronics Control)
      </a>
      extensions.
     </p>
     <p>
      Production of consumer HDMI products started in late 2003.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Europe either DVI-HDCP or HDMI is included in the
      <a href="/wiki/HD_ready" title="HD ready">
       HD ready
      </a>
      in-store labeling specification for TV sets for HDTV, formulated by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Information,_Communications_and_Consumer_Electronics_Technology_Industry_Associations" title="European Information, Communications and Consumer Electronics Technology Industry Associations">
       EICTA
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/SES_Astra" title="SES Astra">
       SES Astra
      </a>
      in 2005. HDMI began to appear on
      <a href="/wiki/Consumer" title="Consumer">
       consumer
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDTV" title="HDTV">
       HDTV
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Camcorder" title="Camcorder">
       camcorders
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_still_camera" title="Digital still camera">
       digital still cameras
      </a>
      in 2006.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of January 8, 2013 (ten years after the release of the first HDMI specification), over 3 billion HDMI devices have been sold.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteJanuary2013_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteJanuary2013-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YahooHDMIJanuary2013CESPress_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-YahooHDMIJanuary2013CESPress-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BusinessHDMIJanuary2013CESPress_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BusinessHDMIJanuary2013CESPress-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

          </a>
         </li>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32">

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The HDMI founders are
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitachi,_Ltd." title="Hitachi, Ltd.">
       Hitachi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">
       Panasonic
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">
       Philips
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Image" title="Silicon Image">
       Silicon Image
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">
       Sony
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomson_SA" title="Thomson SA">
       Thomson, RCA
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">
       Toshiba
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAdopters_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAdopters-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Digital Content Protection, LLC provides
      <a href="/wiki/High-bandwidth_Digital_Content_Protection" title="High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection">
       HDCP
      </a>
      (which was developed by
      <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">
       Intel
      </a>
      ) for HDMI.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI has the support of motion picture producers
      <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">
       Fox
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">
       Universal
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">
       Warner Bros.
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">
       Disney
      </a>
      , along with system operators
      <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">
       DirecTV
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EchoStar_Communications_Corporation" title="EchoStar Communications Corporation">
       EchoStar
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Dish_Network" title="Dish Network">
       Dish Network
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/CableLabs" title="CableLabs">
       CableLabs
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIFAQ_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIFAQ-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The HDMI founders began development on HDMI 1.0 on April 16, 2002, with the goal of creating an AV connector that was backward-compatible with DVI.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIpart1_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIpart1-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIWGpaper_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIWGpaper-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At the time, DVI-HDCP (DVI with HDCP) and DVI-HDTV (DVI-HDCP using the CEA-861-B video standard) were being used on HDTVs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIWGpaper_18-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIWGpaper-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2007WhitePaper_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2007WhitePaper-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI 1.0 was designed to improve on DVI-HDTV by using a smaller connector and adding audio capability and enhanced
      <a href="/wiki/YCbCr" title="YCbCr">
       YCbCr
      </a>
      capability and consumer electronics control functions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIWGpaper_18-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIWGpaper-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2007WhitePaper_19-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2007WhitePaper-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first Authorized Testing Center (ATC), which tests HDMI products, was opened by
      <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Image" title="Silicon Image">
       Silicon Image
      </a>
      on June 23, 2003, in California, United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first ATC in Japan was opened by
      <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">
       Panasonic
      </a>
      on May 1, 2004, in Osaka.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first ATC in Europe was opened by
      <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">
       Philips
      </a>
      on May 25, 2005, in Caen, France.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first ATC in China was opened by Silicon Image on November 21, 2005, in Shenzhen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first ATC in India was opened by Philips on June 12, 2008, in Bangalore.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The HDMI website contains a list of all the ATCs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to In-Stat, the number of HDMI devices sold was 5 million in 2004, 17.4 million in 2005, 63 million in 2006, and 143 million in 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIIn-Stat_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIIn-Stat-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI has become the
      <a href="/wiki/De_facto_standard" title="De facto standard">
       de facto standard
      </a>
      for HDTVs, and according to In-Stat, around 90% of digital televisions in 2007 included HDMI.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIIn-Stat_27-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIIn-Stat-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In-Stat has estimated that 229 million HDMI devices were sold in 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On April 8, 2008 there were over 850
      <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">
       consumer electronics
      </a>
      and PC companies that had adopted the HDMI specification (HDMI Adopters).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2009Future_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2009Future-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On January 7, 2009, HDMI Licensing, LLC announced that HDMI had reached an installed base of over 600 million HDMI devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2009Future_36-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2009Future-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In-Stat has estimated that 394 million HDMI devices will sell in 2009 and that all digital televisions by the end of 2009 would have at least one HDMI input.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2009Future_36-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2009Future-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On January 28, 2008, In-Stat reported that shipments of HDMI were expected to exceed those of DVI in 2008, driven primarily by the consumer electronics market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIIn-Stat_27-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIIn-Stat-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2008,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/PC_Magazine" title="PC Magazine">
        PC Magazine
       </a>
      </i>
      awarded a Technical Excellence Award in the Home Theater category for an "innovation that has changed the world" to the CEC portion of the HDMI specification.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ten companies were given a Technology and Engineering Emmy Award for their development of HDMI by the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Television_Arts_and_Sciences" title="National Academy of Television Arts and Sciences">
       National Academy of Television Arts and Sciences
      </a>
      on January 7, 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On October 25, 2011, the HDMI Forum was established by the HDMI founders to create an open organization so that interested companies can participate in the development of the HDMI specification.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIPressRelease20111025_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIPressRelease20111025-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIForumFAQForum_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIForumFAQForum-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All members of the HDMI Forum have equal voting rights, may participate in the Technical Working Group, and if elected can be on the Board of Directors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIForumFAQForum_41-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIForumFAQForum-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There is no limit to the number of companies allowed in the HDMI Forum though companies must pay an annual fee of $15,000 with an additional annual fee of $5,000 for those companies who serve on the Board of Directors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIForumFAQForum_41-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIForumFAQForum-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Board of Directors will be made up of 11 companies who are elected every 2 years by a general vote of HDMI Forum members.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIForumFAQForum_41-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIForumFAQForum-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All future development of the HDMI specification will take place in the HDMI Forum and will be built upon the HDMI 1.4b specification.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIForumFAQForum_41-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIForumFAQForum-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also on the same day HDMI Licensing, LLC announced that there were over 1,100 HDMI Adopters and that over 2 billion HDMI-enabled products had shipped since the launch of the HDMI standard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAdopters_15-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAdopters-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIPressRelease20111025_40-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIPressRelease20111025-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      From October 25, 2011, all development of the HDMI specification became the responsibility of the newly created HDMI Forum.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIPressRelease20111025_40-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIPressRelease20111025-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On January 8, 2013, HDMI Licensing, LLC announced that there were over 1,300 HDMI Adopters and that over 3 billion HDMI devices had shipped since the launch of the HDMI standard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteJanuary2013_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteJanuary2013-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YahooHDMIJanuary2013CESPress_13-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-YahooHDMIJanuary2013CESPress-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BusinessHDMIJanuary2013CESPress_14-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BusinessHDMIJanuary2013CESPress-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The day also marked the 10-year anniversary of the release of the first HDMI specification.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteJanuary2013_12-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteJanuary2013-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YahooHDMIJanuary2013CESPress_13-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-YahooHDMIJanuary2013CESPress-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BusinessHDMIJanuary2013CESPress_14-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-BusinessHDMIJanuary2013CESPress-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications">
       Specifications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Specifications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDMI_1.3a_Specifications" title="HDMI 1.3a Specifications">
       HDMI 1.3a Specifications
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The HDMI specification defines the protocols, signals, electrical interfaces and mechanical requirements of the standard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The maximum pixel clock rate for HDMI 1.0 was 165MHz, which was sufficient to allow
      <a href="/wiki/1080p" title="1080p">
       1080p
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WUXGA" title="WUXGA">
       WUXGA
      </a>
      (19201200) at 60Hz. HDMI 1.3 increased that to 340MHz, which allows for higher resolution (such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graphic_display_resolutions#WQXGA" title="Graphic display resolutions">
       WQXGA
      </a>
      , 25601600) across a single digital link.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006pr_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006pr-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      An HDMI connection can either be single-link (type A/C/D) or dual-link (type B) and can have a video pixel rate of 25MHz to 340MHz (for a single-link connection) or 25MHz to 680MHz (for a dual-link connection). Video formats with rates below 25MHz (e.g., 13.5MHz for 480i/NTSC) are transmitted using a pixel-repetition scheme.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIFAQ_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIFAQ-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Audio.2Fvideo">
       Audio/video
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Audio/video">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      HDMI uses the
      <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Association" title="Consumer Electronics Association">
       Consumer Electronics Association
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Industries_Alliance" title="Electronic Industries Alliance">
       Electronic Industries Alliance
      </a>
      861 standards. HDMI 1.0 to HDMI 1.2a uses the EIA/CEA-861-B video standard, HDMI 1.3 uses the CEA-861-D video standard, and HDMI 1.4 uses the CEA-861-E video standard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The CEA-861-E document defines "video formats and waveforms; colorimetry and quantization; transport of compressed and uncompressed, as well as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_Pulse_Code_Modulation" title="Linear Pulse Code Modulation">
       Linear Pulse Code Modulation
      </a>
      (LPCM), audio; carriage of auxiliary data; and implementations of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_Electronics_Standards_Association" title="Video Electronics Standards Association">
       Video Electronics Standards Association
      </a>
      (VESA)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extended_display_identification_data#Enhanced_EDID_.28E-EDID.29" title="Extended display identification data">
       Enhanced Extended Display Identification Data Standard
      </a>
      (E-EDID)".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEA-861-E_Standards_Details_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEA-861-E_Standards_Details-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 15, 2013, the CEA announced the publication of CEA-861-F which is a standard that can be used by interfaces such as DVI, HDMI, and LVDS.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEA861FpublishedJuly2013Businesswire_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEA861FpublishedJuly2013Businesswire-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      CEA-861-F adds the ability to transmit several
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultra_high_definition_television" title="Ultra high definition television">
       Ultra HD
      </a>
      video formats and additional color spaces.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEA861FpublishedJuly2013Businesswire_45-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEA861FpublishedJuly2013Businesswire-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      To ensure baseline compatibility between different HDMI sources and displays (as well as backward compatibility with the electrically compatible DVI standard) all HDMI devices must implement the
      <a href="/wiki/SRGB" title="SRGB">
       sRGB
      </a>
      color space at 8 bits per component.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs6.2.3_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs6.2.3-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ability to use the YCbCr color space and higher color depths ("deep color") is optional. HDMI permits sRGB 4:4:4
      <a href="/wiki/Chroma_subsampling" title="Chroma subsampling">
       chroma subsampling
      </a>
      (816 bits per component),
      <a href="/wiki/XvYCC" title="XvYCC">
       xvYCC
      </a>
      4:4:4 chroma subsampling (816 bits per component), YCbCr 4:4:4 chroma subsampling (816 bits per component), or YCbCr 4:2:2 chroma subsampling (812 bits per component).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs6.7.2_47-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs6.7.2-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The color spaces that can be used by HDMI are
      <a href="/wiki/Rec._601" title="Rec. 601">
       ITU-R BT.601
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rec._709" title="Rec. 709">
       ITU-R BT.709-5
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/XvYCC" title="XvYCC">
       IEC 61966-2-4
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs6.7.2_47-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs6.7.2-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For digital audio, if an HDMI device has audio, it is required to implement the baseline format: stereo (uncompressed) PCM. Other formats are optional, with HDMI allowing up to 8 channels of uncompressed audio at sample sizes of 16-bit, 20-bit and 24-bit, with sample rates of 32kHz, 44.1kHz, 48kHz, 88.2kHz, 96kHz, 176.4kHz and 192kHz.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2007WhitePaper_19-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2007WhitePaper-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs7_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs7-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI also carries any
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IEC_61937" title="IEC 61937">
       IEC 61937
      </a>
      -compliant compressed audio stream, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Digital" title="Dolby Digital">
       Dolby Digital
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_Theater_System" title="Digital Theater System">
       DTS
      </a>
      , and up to 8 channels of one-bit
      <a href="/wiki/Direct_Stream_Digital" title="Direct Stream Digital">
       DSD
      </a>
      audio (used on
      <a href="/wiki/Super_Audio_CD" title="Super Audio CD">
       Super Audio CDs
      </a>
      ) at rates up to four times that of Super Audio CD.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs7_49-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs7-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With version 1.3, HDMI allows lossless compressed audio streams
      <a href="/wiki/Dolby_TrueHD" title="Dolby TrueHD">
       Dolby TrueHD
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/DTS-HD_Master_Audio" title="DTS-HD Master Audio">
       DTS-HD Master Audio
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs7_49-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs7-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As with the YCbCr video, audio capability is optional. Audio return channel (ARC) is a feature introduced in the HDMI 1.4 standard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIARC_50-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIARC-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "Return" refers to the case where the audio comes from the TV and can be sent "upstream" to the AV receiver using the HDMI cable connected to the AV receiver.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIARC_50-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIARC-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      An example given on the HDMI website is that a TV that directly receives a terrestrial/satellite broadcast, or has a video source built in, sends the audio "upstream" to the AV receiver.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIARC_50-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIARC-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The HDMI standard was not designed to pass
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Closed_caption" title="Closed caption">
       closed caption
      </a>
      data (for example,
      <a href="/wiki/Subtitle_(captioning)" title="Subtitle (captioning)">
       subtitles
      </a>
      ) to the television for decoding.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As such, any closed caption stream must be decoded and included as an image in the video stream(s) prior to transmission over an HDMI cable to be viewed on the DTV. This limits the caption style (even for digital captions) to only that decoded at the source prior to HDMI transmission. This also prevents closed captions when transmission over HDMI is required for upconversion. For example, a DVD player that sends an upscaled 720p/1080i format via HDMI to an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDTV" title="HDTV">
       HDTV
      </a>
      has no way to pass
      <a href="/wiki/Closed_captioning" title="Closed captioning">
       Closed Captioning
      </a>
      data so that the HDTV can decode it, as there is
      <a href="/wiki/Closed_captioning#HDTV_interoperability_issues" title="Closed captioning">
       no line 21 VBI
      </a>
      in that format.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Uncompressed_video">
       Uncompressed video
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Uncompressed video">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Uncompressed_video" title="Uncompressed video">
       Uncompressed video
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The HDMI specification specifies several modes of uncompressed digital video. Although often
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HD_video" title="HD video">
       HD video
      </a>
      capable cameras include an HDMI interface for playback or even
      <a href="/wiki/Live_preview" title="Live preview">
       live preview
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Image_processor" title="Image processor">
       image processor
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_processor" title="Video processor">
       video processor
      </a>
      of cameras usable for uncompressed video must be able to deliver the full
      <a href="/wiki/Image_resolution" title="Image resolution">
       image resolution
      </a>
      at the specified
      <a href="/wiki/Frame_rate" title="Frame rate">
       frame rate
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Real-time_computing#Real-time_in_Digital_Signal_Processing" title="Real-time computing">
       realtime
      </a>
      without any missing frames causing judder. Therefore, usable uncompressed video out of HDMI is often called "Clean HDMI".
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Communication_channel_protocols">
       Communication channel protocols
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Communication channel protocols">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      HDMI has three physically separate communication channels, which are the DDC, TMDS and the optional CEC.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs8.1_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs8.1-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI 1.4 added ARC and HEC.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteHEC_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteHEC-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="DDC">
       DDC
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: DDC">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Display_Data_Channel" title="Display Data Channel">
       Display Data Channel
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Display_Data_Channel" title="Display Data Channel">
       Display Data Channel
      </a>
      (DDC) is a communication channel based on the
      <a href="/wiki/I%C2%B2C" title="IC">
       IC
      </a>
      bus specification.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs1.2_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs1.2-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs3_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs3-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI specifically requires the device implement the
      <a href="/wiki/Display_Data_Channel#Enhanced_Display_Data_Channel_.28E-DDC.29" title="Display Data Channel">
       Enhanced Display Data Channel
      </a>
      (E-DDC), which is used by the HDMI source device to read the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extended_display_identification_data#Enhanced_EDID_.28E-EDID.29" title="Extended display identification data">
       E-EDID
      </a>
      data from the HDMI sink device to learn what audio/video formats it can take.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs8.1_52-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs8.1-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs1.2_55-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs1.2-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs3_56-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs3-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI requires that the E-DDC implement
      <a href="/wiki/I%C2%B2C" title="IC">
       IC
      </a>
      standard mode speed (100
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kbit/s" title="Kbit/s">
       kbit/s
      </a>
      ) and allows it to optionally implement fast mode speed (400kbit/s).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The DDC channel is actively used for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDCP" title="HDCP">
       High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="TMDS">
       TMDS
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: TMDS">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transition_Minimized_Differential_Signaling" title="Transition Minimized Differential Signaling">
       Transition Minimized Differential Signaling
      </a>
      (TMDS) on HDMI interleaves video, audio and auxiliary data using three different packet types, called the Video Data Period, the Data Island Period and the Control Period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the Video Data Period, the pixels of an active video line are transmitted.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2_58-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the Data Island period (which occurs during the horizontal and vertical blanking intervals), audio and auxiliary data are transmitted within a series of packets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2_58-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Control Period occurs between Video and Data Island periods.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2_58-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Both HDMI and
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_Visual_Interface" title="Digital Visual Interface">
       DVI
      </a>
      use TMDS to send 10-bit characters that are encoded using
      <a href="/wiki/8b/10b_encoding" title="8b/10b encoding">
       8b/10b encoding
      </a>
      that differs from the original IBM form for the Video Data Period and 2b/10b encoding for the Control Period. HDMI adds the ability to send audio and auxiliary data using 4b/10b encoding for the Data Island Period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2_58-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs5.1.2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Each Data Island Period is 32 pixels in size and contains a 32-bit Packet Header, which includes 8 bits of
      <a href="/wiki/BCH_code" title="BCH code">
       BCH
      </a>
      ECC parity data for
      <a href="/wiki/Error_detection_and_correction#Error-correcting_code" title="Error detection and correction">
       error correction
      </a>
      and describes the contents of the packet.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs5.3.1_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs5.3.1-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Each Packet contains four subpackets, and each subpacket is 64 bits in size, including 8 bits of BCH ECC parity data, allowing for each Packet to carry up to 224 bits of audio data.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Each Data Island Period can contain up to 18 Packets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Seven of the 15 Packet types described in the HDMI 1.3a specifications deal with audio data, while the other 8 types deal with auxiliary data.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs5.3.1_59-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs5.3.1-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Among these are the General Control Packet and the Gamut Metadata Packet. The General Control Packet carries information on AVMUTE (which mutes the audio during changes that may cause audio noise) and
      <a href="/wiki/Color_depth" title="Color depth">
       Color Depth
      </a>
      (which sends the bit depth of the current video stream and is required for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_color" title="Deep color">
       deep color
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Gamut Metadata Packet carries information on the
      <a href="/wiki/Color_space" title="Color space">
       color space
      </a>
      being used for the current video stream and is required for xvYCC.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs6.7.2_47-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs6.7.2-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="CEC">
       CEC
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: CEC">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Consumer Electronics Control (CEC) is an HDMI feature designed to allow the user to command and control up-to 15 CEC-enabled devices, that are connected through HDMI,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      by using only one of their remote controls (for example by controlling a
      <a href="/wiki/Television_set" title="Television set">
       television set
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Set-top_box" title="Set-top box">
       set-top box
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/DVD_player" title="DVD player">
       DVD player
      </a>
      using only the remote control of the TV).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsCEC3.1_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsCEC3.1-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      CEC also allows for individual CEC-enabled devices to command and control each other without user intervention.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsCEC3.1_68-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsCEC3.1-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It is a one-wire bidirectional
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serial_communications" title="Serial communications">
       serial
      </a>
      bus that is based on the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Committee_for_Electrotechnical_Standardization" title="European Committee for Electrotechnical Standardization">
       CENELEC
      </a>
      standard
      <a href="/wiki/AV.link" title="AV.link">
       AV.link
      </a>
      protocol to perform
      <a href="/wiki/Remote_control" title="Remote control">
       remote control
      </a>
      functions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      CEC wiring is mandatory, although implementation of CEC in a product is optional.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs8.1_52-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs8.1-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was defined in HDMI Specification 1.0 and updated in HDMI 1.2, HDMI 1.2a and HDMI 1.3a (which added timer and audio commands to the bus).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsCEC3.1_68-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsCEC3.1-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsCEC1.3_73-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsCEC1.3-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      USB to CEC adapters exist that allow a computer to control CEC-enabled devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">
       Trade names
      </a>
      for CEC are Anynet+ (
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">
       Samsung
      </a>
      ), Aquos Link (
      <a href="/wiki/Sharp_Corporation" title="Sharp Corporation">
       Sharp
      </a>
      ), BRAVIA Link and BRAVIA Sync (
      <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">
       Sony
      </a>
      ), HDMI-CEC (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitachi_Ltd." title="Hitachi Ltd.">
       Hitachi
      </a>
      ), E-link (
      <a href="/wiki/AOC_International" title="AOC International">
       AOC
      </a>
      ), Kuro Link (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pioneer_(company)" title="Pioneer (company)">
       Pioneer
      </a>
      ), INlink (
      <a href="/wiki/Insignia" title="Insignia">
       Insignia
      </a>
      ), CE-Link and Regza Link (
      <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">
       Toshiba
      </a>
      ), RIHD (Remote Interactive over HDMI) (
      <a href="/wiki/Onkyo" title="Onkyo">
       Onkyo
      </a>
      ), RuncoLink (
      <a href="/wiki/Runco_International" title="Runco International">
       Runco International
      </a>
      ), SimpLink (
      <a href="/wiki/LG_Electronics" title="LG Electronics">
       LG
      </a>
      ), T-Link (
      <a href="/wiki/ITT_Corporation" title="ITT Corporation">
       ITT
      </a>
      ), HDAVI Control, EZ-Sync, VIERA Link (
      <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">
       Panasonic
      </a>
      ), EasyLink (
      <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">
       Philips
      </a>
      ), and NetCommand for HDMI (
      <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">
       Mitsubishi
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The following is a list of the most commonly used HDMI-CEC commands:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        One Touch Play
       </b>
       allows devices to switch the TV to use it as the active source when playback starts
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        System Standby
       </b>
       enables users to switch multiple devices to standby mode with the press of one button
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Preset Transfer
       </b>
       transfers the tuner channel setup to another TV set
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        One Touch Record
       </b>
       allows users to record whatever is currently being shown on the HDTV screen on a selected recording device
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Timer Programming
       </b>
       allows users to use the
       <a href="/wiki/Electronic_program_guide" title="Electronic program guide">
        electronic program guides
       </a>
       (EPGs) that are built into many HDTVs and set-top-boxes to program the timer in recording devices like PVRs and DVRs
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        System Information
       </b>
       checks all components for bus addresses and configuration
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Deck Control
       </b>
       allows a component to interrogate and control the operation (play, pause, rewind etc.), of a playback component (Blu-ray or HD DVD player or a Camcorder, etc.)
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Tuner Control
       </b>
       allows a component to control the tuner of another component
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        OSD Display
       </b>
       uses the OSD of the TV set to display text
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Device Menu Control
       </b>
       allows a component to control the menu system of another component by passing through the user interface (UI) commands
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Routing Control
       </b>
       controls the switching of signal sources
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Remote Control Pass Through
       </b>
       allows remote control commands to be passed through to other devices within the system
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Device OSD Name Transfer
       </b>
       transfers the preferred device names to the TV set
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        System Audio Control
       </b>
       allows the volume of an AV receiver, integrated amplifier or preamplifier to be controlled using any remote control from a suitably equipped device(s) in the system
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="ARC">
       ARC
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: ARC">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.4 introduces a feature called ARC (Audio Return Channel) among other features.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteHEC_54-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteHEC-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEPROdefinitionHEAC_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEPROdefinitionHEAC-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Like HEC, the ARC feature, this feature use two pins from the connector: a previously unused pin and the hot plug detect pin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEPROdefinitionHEAC_83-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEPROdefinitionHEAC-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-audioholics.com_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-audioholics.com-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ARC is an audio link meant to replace other cables between the TV and the A/V receiver or speaker system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This direction is used when the TV is the one that generates or receives the video stream instead of the other equipment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A typical case is the running of an app on a smart TV such as Netflix, but reproduction of audio is handled by the other equipment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Without ARC, the audio output from the TV needs to be routed by another cable, typically TOS-Link or coax, into the speaker system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cepro.com_85-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cepro.com-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/HDMI#HEC" title="HDMI">
       HEC (HDMI Ethernet Channel)
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/HDMI#ARC" title="HDMI">
       ARC (Audio Return Channel)
      </a>
      support combined by one port or cable is also sometimes referred to as "HEAC" (HDMI Ethernet Audio Control).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEPROdefinitionHEAC_83-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEPROdefinitionHEAC-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="HEC">
       HEC
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: HEC">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.4 introduces a feature called HEC (HDMI Ethernet Channel) among other features.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteHEC_54-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteHEC-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEPROdefinitionHEAC_83-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEPROdefinitionHEAC-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Like ARC, the HEC feature use two pins from the connector: a previously unused pin and the hot plug detect pin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEPROdefinitionHEAC_83-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEPROdefinitionHEAC-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-audioholics.com_84-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-audioholics.com-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI Ethernet Channel technology consolidates video, audio, and data streams into a single HDMI cable, and the HEC feature enables IP-based applications over HDMI and provides a bidirectional Ethernet communication at 100Mbit/s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteHEC_54-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteHEC-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Ethernet_physical_layer" title="Ethernet physical layer">
       physical layer
      </a>
      of the Ethernet implementation uses attenuated
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/100BASE-TX" title="100BASE-TX">
       100BASE-TX
      </a>
      type signals on a single
      <a href="/wiki/Twisted_pair" title="Twisted pair">
       twisted pair
      </a>
      for both transmit and receive.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cepro.com_85-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-cepro.com-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/HDMI#HEC" title="HDMI">
       HEC (HDMI Ethernet Channel)
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/HDMI#ARC" title="HDMI">
       ARC (Audio Return Channel)
      </a>
      support combined by one port or cable is also sometimes refereed to as "HEAC" (HDMI Ethernet Audio Control).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEPROdefinitionHEAC_83-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-CEPROdefinitionHEAC-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Compatibility_with_DVI">
       Compatibility with DVI
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Compatibility with DVI">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg">
        <img alt="An adapter with a DVI receptacle connector to HDMI plug connector." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="2800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg/220px-DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg/330px-DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg/440px-DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DVI-HDMI-Adapter.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An adapter with HDMI (male) and DVI (female) connectors
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg">
        <img alt="An adapter with an HDMI receptacle connector to DVI plug connector with a close up of the HDMI connector." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1600" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg/220px-Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg/330px-Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg/440px-Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adapter_dvi_hdmi_S7302224_wp.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An adapter with DVI and HDMI (female) connectors
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      HDMI is
      <a href="/wiki/Backward_compatibility" title="Backward compatibility">
       backward compatible
      </a>
      with single-link
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_Visual_Interface" title="Digital Visual Interface">
       Digital Visual Interface
      </a>
      digital video (DVI-D or DVI-I, but not DVI-A). No signal conversion is required when an adapter or asymmetric cable is used, so there is no loss of video quality.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsAppC_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsAppC-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From a user's perspective, an HDMI display can be driven by a single-link DVI-D source, since HDMI and DVI-D define an overlapping minimum set of allowed resolutions and framebuffer formats to ensure a basic level of interoperability. In the reverse case a DVI-D monitor would have the same level of basic interoperability unless there are content protection issues with
      <a href="/wiki/High-bandwidth_Digital_Content_Protection" title="High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection">
       High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection
      </a>
      (HDCP) or the HDMI color encoding is in component color space
      <a href="/wiki/YCbCr" title="YCbCr">
       YCbCr
      </a>
      which is not possible in DVI, instead of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RGB" title="RGB">
       RGB
      </a>
      . An HDMI source such as a Blu-ray player may demand HDCP-compliance of the display, and refuse to output HDCP-protected content to a non-compliant display.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A further complication is that there is a small amount of display equipment, such as some high-end home theater projectors, designed with HDMI inputs but not HDCP-compliant.
     </p>
     <p>
      Any DVI-to-HDMI adapter can function as an HDMI-to-DVI adapter (and vice versa). Typically, the only limitation is the
      <a href="/wiki/Gender_of_connectors_and_fasteners" title="Gender of connectors and fasteners">
       gender of the adapter's connectors
      </a>
      and the gender of the cables and sockets it is used with.
     </p>
     <p>
      Features specific to HDMI, such as remote-control and audio transport, are not available in devices that use legacy DVI-D signalling. However, many devices output HDMI over a DVI connector (e.g.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radeon_R600" title="Radeon R600">
       ATI 3000-series
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GeForce_200_Series" title="GeForce 200 Series">
       NVIDIA GTX 200-series
      </a>
      video cards),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsAppC_7-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsAppC-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and some multimedia displays may accept HDMI (including audio) over a DVI input. Exact capabilities beyond basic compatibility vary from product to product. Adapters are generally bi-directional.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Audio">
       Audio
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Audio">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Since the DVI specification does not include audio transport, an interoperability problem arises when an HDMI-source drives a legacy DVI display (such as a PC monitor), or conversely, when a DVI source drives an HDMI display. While HDMI and DVI compliance rules ensure that a DVI video connection can be successfully negotiated and established (via a mutually capable display mode), the audio signal must still be transported through means outside of the DVI connection. Typically, an HDMI-equipped source will provide additional outputs for audio, such as line-level analog and
      <a href="/wiki/S/PDIF" title="S/PDIF">
       S/PDIF
      </a>
      , which provide a baseline audio program (such as
      <a href="/wiki/Pulse-code_modulation" title="Pulse-code modulation">
       stereo PCM
      </a>
      ). Likewise, when displaying video from an HDMI jack, an HDMI-equipped display may allow alternative audio sourcing from a separate pair of analog-audio inputs. Provision for any of these compatibility mechanisms is down to the manufacturer; they are not specified by HDMI. By 2010, nearly all HDMI-equipped sources (set-top and media-extender boxes, Blu-ray and DVD players, and PCs) provided separate analog audio outputs, and many HDMI-equipped televisions were equipped for alternate-audio input when sourcing video from an HDMI input.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Content_protection_.28HDCP.29">
       Content protection (HDCP)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Content protection (HDCP)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/High-bandwidth_Digital_Content_Protection" title="High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection">
       High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection (HDCP) is a newer form of Digital Rights Management. Intel created the original technology to make sure that digital content followed the guidelines set by the Digital Content Protection group.
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI can use
      <a href="/wiki/High-bandwidth_Digital_Content_Protection" title="High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection">
       HDCP
      </a>
      to encrypt the signal if required by the source device.
      <a href="/wiki/Content_Scramble_System" title="Content Scramble System">
       CSS
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Content_Protection_for_Recordable_Media" title="Content Protection for Recordable Media">
       CPRM
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Access_Content_System" title="Advanced Access Content System">
       AACS
      </a>
      require the use of HDCP on HDMI when playing back encrypted
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DVD_Video" title="DVD Video">
       DVD Video
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DVD_Audio" title="DVD Audio">
       DVD Audio
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/HD_DVD" title="HD DVD">
       HD DVD
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">
       Blu-ray Disc
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDCP_Repeater_bit" title="HDCP Repeater bit">
       HDCP Repeater bit
      </a>
      controls the authentication and switching/distribution of an HDMI signal. According to HDCP Specification 1.2 (beginning with HDMI CTS 1.3a), any system that implements HDCP must do so in a fully compliant manner. HDCP testing that was previously only a requirement for optional tests such as the "Simplay HD" testing program is now part of the requirements for HDMI compliance.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20072_90-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20072-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDCP allows for up to 127 devices to be connected, with up to 7 levels, using a combination of sources, sinks and repeaters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDCPSummary_91-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDCPSummary-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A simple example of this is several HDMI devices connected to an HDMI AV receiver that is connected to an HDMI display.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDCPSummary_91-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDCPSummary-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Devices called HDCP strippers can remove the HDCP information from the video signal so the video can play on non-HDCP-compliant displays,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
