       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      though a
      <a href="/wiki/Fair_use" title="Fair use">
       fair use
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-disclosure" title="Non-disclosure">
       non-disclosure
      </a>
      form must usually be signed with a registering agency before use.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Connectors">
       Connectors
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Connectors">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HDMI_Connector.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="398" data-file-width="935" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/HDMI_Connector.jpg/220px-HDMI_Connector.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/HDMI_Connector.jpg/330px-HDMI_Connector.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/HDMI_Connector.jpg/440px-HDMI_Connector.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HDMI_Connector.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        connector types for HDMI
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HDMI.jpg">
        <img alt="A close up image of the end of an HDMI type A plug connector." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="792" data-file-width="1499" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/HDMI.jpg/220px-HDMI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/HDMI.jpg/330px-HDMI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/HDMI.jpg/440px-HDMI.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HDMI.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        HDMI type A plug (male) connector
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:221px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HDMI.socket.png">
        <img alt="An HDMI type A receptacle connector on a device with the words HDMI IN below it." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="259" data-file-width="219" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/HDMI.socket.png" width="219"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HDMI.socket.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        HDMI type A receptacle (female) connector
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      There are five HDMI connector types. Type A/B are defined in the HDMI 1.0 specification, type C is defined in the HDMI 1.3 specification, and type D/E are defined in the HDMI 1.4 specification.
      <span id="HDMI_A">
      </span>
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Type A
      </dt>
      <dd>
       The plug (male) connector outside dimensions are 13.9mm  4.45mm, and the receptacle (female) connector inside dimensions are 14mm  4.55mm.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         93
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are 19 pins, with bandwidth to carry all
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SDTV" title="SDTV">
        SDTV
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EDTV" title="EDTV">
        EDTV
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDTV" title="HDTV">
        HDTV
       </a>
       modes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs6.3_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs6.3-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is electrically compatible with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DVI-D#Single-link_DVI" title="DVI-D">
        single-link DVI-D
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.3_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.3-94">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         94
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      <span id="HDMI_B">
      </span>
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Type B
      </dt>
      <dd>
       This connector is 21.2mm  4.45mm and has 29 pins, carrying six differential pairs instead of three, for use with very high-resolution future displays such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graphic_display_resolutions#WQUXGA" title="Graphic display resolutions">
        WQUXGA
       </a>
       (3,8402,400).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.3_94-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.3-94">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         94
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         95
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is electrically compatible with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DVI-D#Dual-link_DVI" title="DVI-D">
        dual-link DVI-D
       </a>
       , but has not yet been used in any products.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.3_94-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.3-94">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         94
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         96
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the use of the extra three differential pairs is reserved as of 1.3 specification.
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      <span id="HDMI_C">
      </span>
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Type C
      </dt>
      <dd>
       This Mini connector is smaller than the type A plug, measuring 10.42mm  2.42mm but has the same 19-pin configuration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1-97">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         97
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         98
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is intended for portable devices.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIFAQ_4-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMIFAQ-4">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         4
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1_97-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1-97">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         97
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14FAQ_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14FAQ-99">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         99
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The differences are that all positive signals of the differential pairs are swapped with their corresponding shield, the DDC/CEC Ground is assigned to pin 13 instead of pin 17, the CEC is assigned to pin 14 instead of pin 13, and the reserved pin is 17 instead of pin 14.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.10.5_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.10.5-100">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         100
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The type C Mini connector can be connected to a type A connector using a type A-to-type C cable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1_97-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1-97">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         97
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14FAQ_99-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14FAQ-99">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         99
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      <span id="HDMI_D">
      </span>
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Type D
      </dt>
      <dd>
       This Micro connector shrinks the connector size to something resembling a
       <a href="/wiki/USB#Mini_and_Micro" title="USB">
        micro-USB
       </a>
       connector,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14FAQ_99-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14FAQ-99">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         99
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14PressRelease_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14PressRelease-101">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         101
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         102
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       measuring only 6.4mm  2.8mm
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         103
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       For comparison, a micro-USB connector is 6.85mm  1.8mm and a USB Type A connector is 11.5mm  4.5mm. It keeps the standard 19 pins of types A and C, but the pin assignment is different from both.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         104
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      <span id="HDMI_E">
      </span>
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Type E
      </dt>
      <dd>
       The Automotive Connection System
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAutomotive_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAutomotive-105">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         105
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       has a locking tab to keep the cable from vibrating loose and a shell to help prevent moisture and dirt from interfering with the signals. A relay connector is available for connecting standard consumer cables to the automotive type.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAutomotiveMX50_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAutomotiveMX50-106">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         106
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cables">
       Cables
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cables">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Although no maximum length for an HDMI cable is specified, signal
      <a href="/wiki/Attenuation" title="Attenuation">
       attenuation
      </a>
      (dependent on the cable's construction quality and conducting materials) limits usable lengths in practice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMISVarticle_107-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMISVarticle-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigfootfaq_108-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bigfootfaq-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI 1.3 defines two cable categories: Category 1-certified cables, which have been tested at 74.5MHz (which would include resolutions such as 720p60 and 1080i60), and Category 2-certified cables, which have been tested at 340MHz (which would include resolutions such as 1080p60 and 2160p30).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14PressRelease_101-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14PressRelease-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.2.6_109-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.2.6-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI4K_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI4K-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Category 1 HDMI cables are marketed as "Standard" and Category 2 HDMI cables as "High Speed".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIFAQ_4-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIFAQ-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This labeling guideline for HDMI cables went into effect on October 17, 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Category 1 and 2 cables can either meet the required parameter specifications for interpair skew, far-end crosstalk, attenuation and differential impedance, or they can meet the required nonequalized/equalized eye diagram requirements.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.2.6_109-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.2.6-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A cable of about 5 meters (16 feet) can be manufactured to Category 1 specifications easily and inexpensively by using 28
      <a href="/wiki/American_wire_gauge" title="American wire gauge">
       AWG
      </a>
      (0.081mm) conductors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMISVarticle_107-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMISVarticle-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With better quality construction and materials, including 24AWG (0.205mm) conductors, an HDMI cable can reach lengths of up to 15 meters (49 feet).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMISVarticle_107-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMISVarticle-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many HDMI cables under 5meters of length that were made before the HDMI 1.3 specification can work as Category 2 cables, but only Category 2-tested cables are guaranteed to work for Category 2 purposes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of the HDMI 1.4 specification, the following cable types are defined for HDMI in general:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Standard HDMI Cable  up to
       <a href="/wiki/1080i" title="1080i">
        1080i
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/720p" title="720p">
        720p
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       Standard HDMI Cable with Ethernet
      </li>
      <li>
       Automotive HDMI Cable
      </li>
      <li>
       High Speed HDMI Cable 
       <a href="/wiki/1080p" title="1080p">
        1080p
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">
        4K
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/3D_television" title="3D television">
        3D
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_color" title="Deep color">
        deep color
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       High Speed HDMI Cable with Ethernet
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      An HDMI cable is usually composed of four shielded
      <a href="/wiki/Twisted_pair" title="Twisted pair">
       twisted pairs
      </a>
      , with impedance of the order of 100
      <a href="/wiki/Ohm" title="Ohm">
       
      </a>
      , plus several separate conductors.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Extenders">
       Extenders
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Extenders">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      An HDMI extender is a single device (or pair of devices) powered with an external power source or with the 5V DC from the HDMI source.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMILongCableLengths_116-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMILongCableLengths-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-XCAT-250_117-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-XCAT-250-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIFiberExtender_118-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIFiberExtender-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Long cables can cause instability of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDCP" title="HDCP">
       HDCP
      </a>
      and blinking on the screen, due to the weakened
      <a href="/wiki/Display_Data_Channel" title="Display Data Channel">
       DDC
      </a>
      signal that HDCP requires. HDCP DDC signals must be multiplexed with TMDS video signals to be compliant with HDCP requirements for HDMI extenders based on a single
      <a href="/wiki/Category_5_cable" title="Category 5 cable">
       Category 5
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Category_6_cable" title="Category 6 cable">
       Category 6 cable
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDCPLicense_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDCPLicense-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several companies offer
      <a href="/wiki/Amplifier" title="Amplifier">
       amplifiers
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Equalization" title="Equalization">
       equalizers
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Repeater" title="Repeater">
       repeaters
      </a>
      that can string several standard HDMI cables together. Active HDMI cables use electronics within the cable to boost the signal and allow for HDMI cables of up to 30 meters (98 feet).,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMILongCableLengths_116-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMILongCableLengths-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      those based on
      <a href="/wiki/HDBaseT" title="HDBaseT">
       HDBaseT
      </a>
      can extend to 100 meters, HDMI extenders that are based on dual
      <a href="/wiki/Category_5_cable" title="Category 5 cable">
       Category 5
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Category_6_cable" title="Category 6 cable">
       Category 6 cable
      </a>
      can extend HDMI to 250 meters (820 feet), while HDMI extenders based on
      <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">
       optical fiber
      </a>
      can extend HDMI to 300 meters (980 feet).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-XCAT-250_117-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-XCAT-250-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIFiberExtender_118-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIFiberExtender-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cost">
       Cost
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cost">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      HDMI manufacturers pay an annual fee of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">
       US$
      </a>
      10,000 plus a royalty rate of $0.15 per unit, reduced to $0.05 if the HDMI logo is used, and further reduced to $0.04 if HDCP is also implemented.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdmiterms_121-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hdmiterms-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      An alternative fee for HDMI manufacturers making fewer than 10,000 units per year is an annual fee of $5,000 with a royalty rate of $1 per unit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdmiterms_121-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-hdmiterms-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The royalty only applies to final products and does not apply to products that are included in, or with, a licensed HDMI product that is already subject to the royalty.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdmiterms_121-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-hdmiterms-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For example, an HDMI cable sold directly to consumers is paid for by the cable manufacturer; however, if the cable manufacturer sells the HDMI cable to a HDTV manufacturer (who then includes the cable with with an HDTV subject to the royalty) then the HDTV manufacturer pays only the royalty on the HDTV.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdmiterms_121-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-hdmiterms-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Versions">
       Versions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Versions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      HDMI devices are manufactured to adhere to various versions of the specification, in which each version is given a number and/or letter, such as 1.0, 1.2, or 1.4b.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Each subsequent version of the specification uses the same kind of cable but increases the
      <a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing)" title="Bandwidth (computing)">
       bandwidth
      </a>
      and/or capabilities of what can be transmitted over the cable.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A product listed as having an HDMI version does not necessarily mean that it will have all of the features that are listed for that version,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      since some HDMI features are optional, such as deep color and xvYCC (which is branded by Sony as "x.v.Color").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIhometoys_123-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIhometoys-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Note that with the release of the version 1.4 cable, the HDMI Licensing LLC group (which oversees the HDMI standard) will require that any reference to version numbers be removed from all packaging and advertising for the cable.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Non-cable HDMI products starting on January 1, 2012 will no longer be allowed to reference the HDMI number and will be required to state which features of the HDMI specification the product implements.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2009TradeLogoGuidelines_126-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2009TradeLogoGuidelines-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Version_1.0">
       Version 1.0
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Version 1.0">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       HDMI 1.0
      </i>
      was released December 9, 2002 and is a single-cable digital audio/video connector interface with a maximum TMDS bandwidth of 4.95
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gbit/s" title="Gbit/s">
       Gbit/s
      </a>
      . It defines up to 3.96Gbit/s of video bandwidth (1080p/60Hz or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UXGA" title="UXGA">
       UXGA
      </a>
      ) and 8channel
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_pulse_code_modulation" title="Linear pulse code modulation">
       LPCM
      </a>
      /192
      <a href="/wiki/Hertz" title="Hertz">
       kHz
      </a>
      /24-bit audio.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Version_1.1">
       Version 1.1
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Version 1.1">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       HDMI 1.1
      </i>
      was released on May 20, 2004 and added
      <a href="/wiki/DVD-Audio" title="DVD-Audio">
       DVD-Audio
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Version_1.2">
       Version 1.2
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Version 1.2">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       HDMI 1.2
      </i>
      was released August 8, 2005 and added the option of One Bit Audio, used on
      <a href="/wiki/Super_Audio_CD" title="Super Audio CD">
       Super Audio CDs
      </a>
      , at up to 8 channels. It also added the availability of HDMI type A connectors for PC sources, the ability for PC sources to implement only the sRGB color space while retaining the option to implement the YCbCr color space, and required HDMI 1.2 and later displays to allow low-voltage sources.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs6.2.3_46-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs6.2.3-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       HDMI 1.2a
      </i>
      was released on December 14, 2005 and fully specifies Consumer Electronic Control (CEC) features, command sets and CEC compliance tests.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Version_1.3">
       Version 1.3
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Version 1.3">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDMI_1.3a_Specifications" title="HDMI 1.3a Specifications">
       HDMI 1.3a Specifications
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.3 was released June 22, 2006 and increased the single-link bandwidth to 340MHz (10.2Gbit/s).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006pr_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006pr-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It optionally allows
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_color" title="Deep color">
       deep color
      </a>
      , with 30-bit, 36-bit and 48-bit
      <a href="/wiki/XvYCC" title="XvYCC">
       xvYCC
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/SRGB" title="SRGB">
       sRGB
      </a>
      , or YCbCr, compared to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/True_Color" title="True Color">
       24-bit
      </a>
      sRGB or YCbCr in previous HDMI versions. It also optionally allows output of
      <a href="/wiki/Dolby_TrueHD" title="Dolby TrueHD">
       Dolby TrueHD
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/DTS-HD_Master_Audio" title="DTS-HD Master Audio">
       DTS-HD Master Audio
      </a>
      streams for external decoding by AV receivers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It incorporates automatic audio syncing (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audio_video_sync" title="Audio video sync">
       audio video sync
      </a>
      ) capability.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006pr_43-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006pr-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It defined cable Categories 1 and 2, with Category 1 cable being tested up to 74.25
      <a href="/wiki/Hertz" title="Hertz">
       MHz
      </a>
      and Category 2 being tested up to 340
      <a href="/wiki/Hertz" title="Hertz">
       MHz
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.2.6_109-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.2.6-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also added the new type C Mini connector for portable devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1_97-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs4.1.1-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.3a was released on November 10, 2006 and had Cable and Sink modifications for type C, source termination recommendations, and removed undershoot and maximum rise/fall time limits.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also changed CEC capacitance limits, clarified sRGB video quantization range, and CEC commands for timer control were brought back in an altered form, with audio control commands added.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also added the optional ability to stream SACD in its bitstream DST format rather than uncompressed raw DSD like from HDMI 1.2 onwards.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsDRH_5-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsDRH-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.3b, 1.3b1 and 1.3c were released on March 26, 2007, November 9, 2007, and August 25, 2008 respectively. They do not introduce differences on HDMI features, functions, or performance,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIRevisionsfor1.3_130-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIRevisionsfor1.3-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but only describe testing for products based on the HDMI 1.3a specification regarding HDMI compliance (1.3b
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20072_90-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20072-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20071_131-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20071-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20073_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20073-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ), the HDMI type C Mini connector (1.3b1
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20072_90-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20072-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20071_131-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20071-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20073_132-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20073-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ) and active HDMI cables (1.3c
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMILongCableLengths_116-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMILongCableLengths-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI200808ComplianceTesting_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI200808ComplianceTesting-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIRevisionsfor1.3_130-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIRevisionsfor1.3-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Version_1.4">
       Version 1.4
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Version 1.4">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="518" data-file-width="692" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png/220px-HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png/330px-HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png/440px-HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HDMI_1.4_with_Audio_Return_Channel.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        HDMI 1.4 with audio return channel
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.4 was released on May 28, 2009, and the first HDMI 1.4 products were available in the second half of 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14PressRelease_101-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14PressRelease-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SiliconImageHDMIVersion14_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SiliconImageHDMIVersion14-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI 1.4 increases the maximum resolution to
      <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">
       4K2K
      </a>
      , i.e. 40962160 at 24Hz (which is a resolution used with
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinema" title="Digital cinema">
       digital theaters
      </a>
      ) or 38402160 (Ultra HD) at 24Hz/25Hz/30Hz; adds an HDMI Ethernet Channel (HEC), which allows for a 100
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mbit/s" title="Mbit/s">
       Mbit/s
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Ethernet" title="Ethernet">
       Ethernet
      </a>
      connection between the two HDMI connected devices so they can share an Internet connection;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteHEC_54-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteHEC-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and introduces an audio return channel (ARC),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIwebsiteARC_53-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIwebsiteARC-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      3D Over HDMI, a new Micro HDMI Connector, expanded set of color spaces, with the addition of sYCC601,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adobe_RGB" title="Adobe RGB">
       Adobe RGB
      </a>
      and Adobe YCC601; and an Automotive Connection System.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14PressRelease_101-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14PressRelease-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14Introduction_135-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14Introduction-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IntroducingHDMIVersion143DPage_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IntroducingHDMIVersion143DPage-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IntroducingHDMIVersion144KSupportPage_137-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IntroducingHDMIVersion144KSupportPage-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI14SpecificationFeatures_138-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI14SpecificationFeatures-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI 1.4 defines several
      <a href="/wiki/Stereoscopy" title="Stereoscopy">
       stereoscopic 3D
      </a>
      formats including field alternative (interlaced), frame packing (a full resolution top-bottom format), line alternative full, side-by-side half, side-by-side full,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2D_plus_depth" title="2D plus depth">
       2D + depth
      </a>
      , and 2D + depth + graphics + graphics depth (
      <a href="/wiki/WOWvx" title="WOWvx">
       WOWvx
      </a>
      ),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14FAQ_99-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14FAQ-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14LaunchDocument_139-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14LaunchDocument-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14UpdateDocument_140-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14UpdateDocument-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with additional top/bottom formats added in version 1.4a. HDMI 1.4 requires that 3D displays implement the frame packing 3D format at either 720p50 and 1080p24 or 720p60 and 1080p24.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14UpdateDocument_140-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14UpdateDocument-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      High Speed HDMI 1.3 cables work with all HDMI 1.4 features except for the HDMI Ethernet Channel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14FAQ_99-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14FAQ-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14LaunchDocument_139-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14LaunchDocument-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14UpdateDocument_140-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14UpdateDocument-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.4a was released on March 4, 2010 and adds two additional mandatory 3D formats for broadcast content, which was deferred with HDMI 1.4 in order to see the direction of the 3D broadcast market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14aPressRelease_141-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14aPressRelease-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14a20100305_142-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14a20100305-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI 1.4a has defined mandatory 3D formats for broadcast, game, and movie content.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14aPressRelease_141-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14aPressRelease-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      HDMI 1.4a requires that 3D displays implement the frame packing 3D format at either 720p50 and 1080p24 or 720p60 and 1080p24, side-by-side horizontal at either 1080i50 or 1080i60, and top-and-bottom at either 720p50 and 1080p24 or 720p60 and 1080p24.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIVersion14a20100305_142-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIVersion14a20100305-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI 1.4b was released on October 11, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAnnouncement20111011_143-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAnnouncement20111011-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One of the new features is that it adds the ability to carry 3D 1080p video at 120Hz  allowing frame packing 3D format at 1080p60 per Eye (120Hz total).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI_1.4b_demystified_by_David_Silberstein_144-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI_1.4b_demystified_by_David_Silberstein-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All future versions of the HDMI specification will be made by the HDMI Forum that was created on October 25, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIPressRelease20111025_40-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIPressRelease20111025-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIForumFAQVersion_145-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIForumFAQVersion-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Version_2.0">
       Version 2.0
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Version 2.0">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      HDMI 2.0, referred to by some manufacturers as HDMI
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultra_high_definition_television" title="Ultra high definition television">
       UHD
      </a>
      , was released on September 4, 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013_146-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI 2.0 increases the maximum TMDS per channel
      <a href="/wiki/Throughput" title="Throughput">
       throughput
      </a>
      from 3.4 Gbit/s to 6 Gbit/s which allows for a maximum total TMDS throughput of 18 Gbit/s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013_146-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This allows HDMI 2.0 to carry
      <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">
       4K resolution
      </a>
      at 60
      <a href="/wiki/Frame_rate" title="Frame rate">
       frames per second
      </a>
      (fps).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013_146-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other features of HDMI 2.0 include the options of the
      <a href="/wiki/Rec._2020" title="Rec. 2020">
       Rec. 2020
      </a>
      color space, Dual View, 4:2:0 chroma subsampling, 25 fps 3D formats, up to 32 channels of audio, up to 1536kHz audio (for example 7.1 channels of 192kHz), up to 4 audio streams, 21:9 aspect ratio, the
      <a href="/wiki/High-Efficiency_Advanced_Audio_Coding" title="High-Efficiency Advanced Audio Coding">
       HE-AAC
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_Resolution_Adaptation" title="Dynamic Resolution Adaptation">
       DRA
      </a>
      audio standards, dynamic auto lip-sync, improved 3D capability, and additional CEC functions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013_146-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2PressReleaseSeptember2013-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI 2.0a was released on April 8, 2015 and added support for
      <a href="/wiki/High-dynamic-range_imaging" title="High-dynamic-range imaging">
       high dynamic range
      </a>
      (HDR) video.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI20aReleasedTwice_149-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI20aReleasedTwice-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Version_comparison">
       Version comparison
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Version comparison">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Note that a given product may choose to implement a subset of the given HDMI version. Certain features such as deep color and xvYCC are optional.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIhometoys_123-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIhometoys-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-153">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-153">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         36-bit capability is mandatory for deep-color-compatible consumer electronic devices, with 48-bit capability being optional.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
          <a href="#cite_note-152">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           152
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-156">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-156">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Maximum resolution is based on
         <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Video_Timings" title="Coordinated Video Timings">
          CVT-RB
         </a>
         , which is a
         <a href="/wiki/VESA" title="VESA">
          VESA
         </a>
         standard for non-CRT-based displays.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
          <a href="#cite_note-154">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           153
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         Using CVT-RB 19201200hz/60hz would have a video bandwidth of 4.63Gbit/s, 25601600p/60hz would have a video bandwidth of 8.07Gbit/s, 40962160p/30hz would have a video bandwidth of 8.40Gbit/s, and 40962160p/60hz would have a video bandwidth of 17.04Gbit/s. All values include TMDS 8b/10b encoding overhead.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
          <a href="#cite_note-155">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           154
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>

        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2IntroductionSeptember2013_165-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2IntroductionSeptember2013-165">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          159
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-yes" style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        Yes
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        2 video streams (Dual View)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2IntroductionSeptember2013_165-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2IntroductionSeptember2013-165">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          159
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        No
       </td>
       <td class="table-yes" style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">
        Yes
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        21:9 aspect ratio
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2IntroductionSeptember2013_165-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2IntroductionSeptember2013-165">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          159
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">

       </td>
       <td class="table-no" style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;">

       </td>

       </td>

     </table>
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">

        </span>
