     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">
       Applications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Applications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Blu-ray_Disc_and_HD_DVD_players">
       Blu-ray Disc and HD DVD players
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Blu-ray Disc and HD DVD players">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">
       Blu-ray Disc
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/HD_DVD" title="HD DVD">
       HD DVD
      </a>
      , introduced in 2006, offer high-fidelity audio features that require HDMI for best results. HDMI 1.3 can transport
      <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Digital_Plus" title="Dolby Digital Plus">
       Dolby Digital Plus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dolby_TrueHD" title="Dolby TrueHD">
       Dolby TrueHD
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/DTS-HD_Master_Audio" title="DTS-HD Master Audio">
       DTS-HD Master Audio
      </a>
      bitstreams in compressed form.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006Specs7_49-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006Specs7-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This capability allows for an
      <a href="/wiki/AV_receiver" title="AV receiver">
       AV receiver
      </a>
      with the necessary decoder to decode the compressed audio stream. The Blu-ray specification does not include video encoded with either deep color or xvYCC; thus, HDMI 1.0 can transfer Blu-ray discs at full video quality.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The HDMI 1.4 specification (released in 2009) added support for 3D video and is used by all Blu-ray 3D compatible players.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Blu-ray Disc Association (BDA) spokespersons have stated (Sept. 2014 at IFA show in Berlin, German) that the Blu-ray 4K/Ultra HD players and UHD discs are expected to be available starting in the second half to 2015. It is anticipated that such Blu-ray UHD players will be required to include a HDMI 2.0 output supporting HDCP 2.2.
     </p>
     <p>
      Blu-ray permits secondary audio decoding, whereby the disc content can tell the player to mix multiple audio sources together before final output.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some Blu-ray and HD DVD players can decode all of the audio codecs internally and can output
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_pulse_code_modulation" title="Linear pulse code modulation">
       LPCM
      </a>
      audio over HDMI. Multichannel LPCM can be transported over an HDMI connection, and as long as the
      <a href="/wiki/AV_receiver" title="AV receiver">
       AV receiver
      </a>
      implements multichannel LPCM audio over HDMI and implements
      <a href="/wiki/High-bandwidth_Digital_Content_Protection" title="High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection">
       HDCP
      </a>
      , the audio reproduction is equal in resolution to HDMI 1.3 bitstream output. Some low-cost AV receivers, such as the Onkyo TX-SR506, do not allow audio processing over HDMI and are labelled as "HDMI pass through" devices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      [10/2014 Update] Virtually all modern AV Receivers now offer HDMI 1.4 inputs and output(s) with processing for all of the audio formats offered by Blu-ray Discs and other HD video sources. During 2014 several manufacturers introduced premium AV Receivers that include one, or multiple, HDMI 2.0 inputs along with a HDMI 2.0 output(s). As of this update, among the major manufacturers of AV receivers only Onkyo/Integra offers such AV Receivers that support both HDMI 2.0 and HDCP 2.2 as will be needed to support certain of the high quality 4K/UHD video sources, such as the upcoming Blu-ray 4K/UHD players.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_cameras_and_camcorders">
       Digital cameras and camcorders
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Digital cameras and camcorders">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      As of 2012, most consumer camcorders, as well as many digital cameras, are equipped with a mini-HDMI connector (type C connector).
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2014, some cameras also have 4K capability and 3D, even for the camera price less than $900. It needs at least a TV/monitor with HDMI 1.4a port.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_computers">
       Personal computers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Personal computers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">
       PCs
      </a>
      with a DVI interface are capable of video output to an HDMI-enabled monitor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMI2006SpecsAppC_7-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMI2006SpecsAppC-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">
       PCs
      </a>
      include an HDMI interface and may also be capable of HDMI audio output, depending on specific hardware.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIIntel_173-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIIntel-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For example, Intel's motherboard chipsets since the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intel_P965_Express" title="Intel P965 Express">
       945G
      </a>
      and NVIDIAs GeForce 8200/8300 motherboard chipsets are capable of 8-channel
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_pulse_code_modulation" title="Linear pulse code modulation">
       LPCM
      </a>
      output over HDMI.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIIntel_173-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIIntel-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAudio2008_174-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAudio2008-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Eight-channel LPCM audio output over HDMI with a video card was first seen with the ATI Radeon HD 4850, which was released in June 2008 and is implemented by other video cards in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radeon_R700" title="Radeon R700">
       ATI Radeon HD 4000 series
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAudio2008_174-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAudio2008-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        169
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
       <a href="#cite_note-176">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        170
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
       <a href="#cite_note-177">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        171
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
       <a href="#cite_note-178">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        172
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">
       Linux
      </a>
      can drive 8-channel LPCM audio over HDMI if the video card has the necessary hardware and implements the
      <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Linux_Sound_Architecture" title="Advanced Linux Sound Architecture">
       Advanced Linux Sound Architecture
      </a>
      (ALSA).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATIR700ALSA_179-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ATIR700ALSA-179">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The ATI Radeon HD 4000 series implements ALSA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATIR700ALSA_179-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ATIR700ALSA-179">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
       <a href="#cite_note-180">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        174
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cyberlink announced in June 2008 that they would update their PowerDVD playback software to allow 192kHz/24-bit Blu-ray Disc audio decoding in Q3-Q4 of 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcard_PowerDVD_181-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcard_PowerDVD-181">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        175
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Corel's WinDVD 9 Plus currently can has 96kHz/24-bit Blu-ray Disc audio decoding.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcard_WinDVD_182-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcard_WinDVD-182">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        176
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Even with an HDMI output, a computer may not be able to produce signals that implement
      <a href="/wiki/High-bandwidth_Digital_Content_Protection" title="High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection">
       HDCP
      </a>
      , Microsoft's Protected Video Path, or Microsoft's Protected Audio Path.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAudio2008_174-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAudio2008-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MicrosoftPVPandPAP_183-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MicrosoftPVPandPAP-183">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        177
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several early graphic cards were labelled as "HDCP-enabled" but did not have the hardware needed for HDCP;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDCP-enabled_184-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDCP-enabled-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      this included some graphic cards based on the ATI X1600 chipset and certain models of the NVIDIA Geforce 7900 series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDCP-enabled_184-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDCP-enabled-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first computer monitors that could process HDCP were released in 2005; by February 2006 a dozen different models had been released.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
       <a href="#cite_note-185">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        179
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
       <a href="#cite_note-186">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        180
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Protected Video Path was enabled in graphic cards that had HDCP capability, since it was required for output of Blu-ray Disc video. In comparison, the Protected Audio Path was required only if a lossless audio bitstream (such as Dolby TrueHD or
      <a href="/wiki/DTS-HD_Master_Audio" title="DTS-HD Master Audio">
       DTS-HD MA
      </a>
      ) was output.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAudio2008_174-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAudio2008-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Uncompressed LPCM audio, however, does not require a Protected Audio Path, and software programs such as PowerDVD and WinDVD can decode Dolby TrueHD and DTS-HD MA and output it as LPCM.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAudio2008_174-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAudio2008-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcard_PowerDVD_181-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcard_PowerDVD-181">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        175
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcard_WinDVD_182-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcard_WinDVD-182">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        176
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A limitation is that if the computer does not implement a Protected Audio Path, the audio must be downsampled to 16-bit 48kHz but can still output at up to 8channels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAudio2008_174-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAudio2008-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      No graphic cards were released in 2008 that implemented the Protected Audio Path.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIAudio2008_174-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIAudio2008-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Asus" title="Asus">
       Asus
      </a>
      Xonar HDAV1.3 became the first HDMI sound card that implemented the Protected Audio Path and could both bitstream and decode lossless audio (Dolby TrueHD and DTS-HD MA), although bitstreaming is only available if using the ArcSoft TotalMedia Theatre software.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcard_187-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcard-187">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        181
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcardupdate_188-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcardupdate-188">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        182
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It has an HDMI 1.3 input/output, and Asus says that it can work with most video cards on the market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcard_187-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcard-187">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        181
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDMIsoundcardupdate_188-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDMIsoundcardupdate-188">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        182
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
       <a href="#cite_note-189">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        183
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
       <div style="margin:0px 2em;">
        <p>
         Legacy interfaces such as VGA, DVI and LVDS have not kept pace, and newer standards such as DisplayPort and HDMI clearly provide the best connectivity options moving forward. In our opinion, DisplayPort 1.2 is the future interface for PC monitors, along with HDMI 1.4a for TV connectivity.
        </p>
       </div>
       <div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">
        
       </div>
       <div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">
        
       </div>
      </div>
      <div style="text-align: left;">
       <span class="citation web">
        <a class="external text" href="http://newsroom.intel.com/community/intel_newsroom/blog/2010/12/08/leading-pc-companies-move-to-all-digital-display-technology-phasing-out-analog" rel="nofollow">
         "Leading PC Companies Move to All Digital Display Technology, Phasing out Analog"
        </a>
        . Intel. December 8, 2010
        <span class="reference-accessdate">
         . Retrieved
         <span class="nowrap">
          September 14,
         </span>
         2012
        </span>
        .
       </span>
       <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHDMI&amp;rft.btitle=Leading+PC+Companies+Move+to+All+Digital+Display+Technology%2C+Phasing+out+Analog&amp;rft.date=December+8%2C+2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnewsroom.intel.com%2Fcommunity%2Fintel_newsroom%2Fblog%2F2010%2F12%2F08%2Fleading-pc-companies-move-to-all-digital-display-technology-phasing-out-analog&amp;rft.pub=Intel&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
        <span style="display:none;">
        </span>
       </span>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In September 2009,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD" title="AMD">
       AMD
      </a>
      announced the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radeon_R800" title="Radeon R800">
       ATI Radeon HD 5000 series
      </a>
      video cards, which have HDMI 1.3 output (deep color, xvYCC wide gamut capability and high bit rate audio), 8-channel LPCM over HDMI, and an integrated HD audio controller with a Protected Audio Path that allows bitstream output over HDMI for AAC, Dolby AC-3, Dolby TrueHD and DTS Master Audio formats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5870GPUSummary_190-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-5870GPUSummary-190">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5850GPUSummary_191-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-5850GPUSummary-191">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        185
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5870Review_192-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-5870Review-192">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        186
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The ATI Radeon HD 5870 released in September 2009 is the first video card that allows bitstream output over HDMI for Dolby TrueHD and DTS-HD Master Audio.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5870Review_192-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-5870Review-192">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        186
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD" title="AMD">
       AMD
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Radeon_HD_6000_Series" title="Radeon HD 6000 Series">
       Radeon HD 6000 Series
      </a>
      implements HDMI 1.4a. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD" title="AMD">
       AMD
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Radeon_HD_7000_Series" title="Radeon HD 7000 Series">
       Radeon HD 7000 Series
      </a>
      implements HDMI 1.4b.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
       <a href="#cite_note-193">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        187
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In December 2010, it was announced that several computer vendors and display makers including
      <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">
       Intel
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMD" title="AMD">
       AMD
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">
       Dell
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lenovo" title="Lenovo">
       Lenovo
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">
       Samsung
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/LG_Display" title="LG Display">
       LG
      </a>
      would stop using
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LVDS" title="LVDS">
       LVDS
      </a>
      (actually,
      <a href="/wiki/FPD-Link" title="FPD-Link">
       FPD-Link
      </a>
      ) from 2013 and legacy
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_Visual_Interface" title="Digital Visual Interface">
       DVI
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VGA" title="VGA">
       VGA
      </a>
      connectors from 2015, replacing them with
      <a href="/wiki/DisplayPort" title="DisplayPort">
       DisplayPort
      </a>
      and HDMI.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
       <a href="#cite_note-194">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        188
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
       <a href="#cite_note-195">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        189
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On August 27, 2012,
      <a href="/wiki/Asus" title="Asus">
       Asus
      </a>
      announced a new 27in (69cm) monitor which can produce its native resolution of 25601440 via HDMI 1.4.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
       <a href="#cite_note-196">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        190
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
       <a href="#cite_note-197">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        191
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On September 18, 2014, Nvidia launched GeForce GTX 980 and GTX 970 (with GM204 chip) with HDMI 2.0 support. On January 22, 2015, GeForce GTX 960 (with GM206 chip) launched with HDMI 2.0 support. On March 17, 2015, GeForce GTX TITAN X(GM200) launched with HDMI 2.0 support. On June 1, 2015, GeForce GTX 980 Ti (with GM200 chip) launched with HDMI 2.0 support.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tablet_computers">
       Tablet computers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Tablet computers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Some
      <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">
       Tablet computers
      </a>
      , such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Surface" title="Microsoft Surface">
       Microsoft Surface
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Xoom" title="Motorola Xoom">
       Motorola Xoom
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_PlayBook" title="BlackBerry PlayBook">
       BlackBerry PlayBook
      </a>
      , Vizio Vtab 1008 and Acer Iconia Tab A500, implement HDMI using Micro-HDMI (Type D) ports. Others, such as the ASUS
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eee_Pad" title="Eee Pad">
       Eee Pad
      </a>
      Transformer implement the standard using Mini-HDMI (Type C) ports. All
      <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">
       iPad
      </a>
      models have a special A/V adapter that converts Apple's data line to a standard HDMI (Type A) port. Samsung has a similar proprietary thirty-pin port for their
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galaxy_Tab_10.1" title="Galaxy Tab 10.1">
       Galaxy Tab 10.1
      </a>
      that can adapt to HDMI as well as USB drives. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dell_Streak_5" title="Dell Streak 5">
       Dell Streak 5
      </a>
      smartphone/tablet hybrid is capable of outputting over HDMI. While the Streak uses a
      <a href="/wiki/PDMI" title="PDMI">
       PDMI
      </a>
      port, a separate cradle is available which adds HDMI compatibility. Most of the Chinese-made tablets running
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Android_OS" title="Android OS">
       Android OS
      </a>
      provide HDMI output using a Mini-HDMI (Type C) port. Most new laptops and desktops now have built in HDMI as well.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_phones">
       Mobile phones
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mobile phones">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Many recent mobile phones can produce output of HDMI video via either a micro-HDMI connector or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_High-definition_Link" title="Mobile High-definition Link">
       MHL
      </a>
      output.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
       <a href="#cite_note-198">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        192
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
       <a href="#cite_note-199">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        193
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
       <a href="#cite_note-200">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        194
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
       <a href="#cite_note-201">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        195
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
       <a href="#cite_note-202">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        196
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
       <a href="#cite_note-203">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        197
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
       <a href="#cite_note-204">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        198
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_compatibility">
       Legacy compatibility
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Legacy compatibility">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      HDMI can only be used with older analog-only devices (using connections such as
      <a href="/wiki/SCART" title="SCART">
       SCART
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VGA" title="VGA">
       VGA
      </a>
      , RCA, etc.) by means of a
      <a href="/wiki/Digital-to-analog_converter" title="Digital-to-analog converter">
       digital-to-analog converter
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/AV_receiver" title="AV receiver">
       AV receiver
      </a>
      , as the interface does not carry any analog signals (unlike DVI, where devices with DVI-I ports accept or provide either digital or analog signals). Cables are available that contain the necessary electronics, but it is important to distinguish these
      <i>
       active
      </i>
      converter cables from
      <i>
       passive
      </i>
      HDMI to VGA cables (which are typically cheaper as they don't include any electronics). The passive cables are
      <i>
       only
      </i>
      useful if you have a device that is generating or expecting HDMI signals on a VGA connector, or VGA signals on an HDMI connector; this is a non-standard feature, not implemented by most devices.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_DisplayPort">
       Relationship with DisplayPort
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Relationship with DisplayPort">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="708" height="88" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg/150px-DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg/225px-DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg/300px-DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg.png 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DisplayPort_plus_plus.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Dual-mode DisplayPort logo
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Another audio/video interface is
      <a href="/wiki/DisplayPort" title="DisplayPort">
       DisplayPort
      </a>
      , version 1.0 of which was approved in May 2006. Several models of display, computer, and video card have DisplayPort ports. The DisplayPort website states that DisplayPort is expected to complement HDMI.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
       <a href="#cite_note-205">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        199
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most of the
      <a href="/wiki/DisplayPort#Supporters" title="DisplayPort">
       companies producing equipment that uses DisplayPort
      </a>
      are in the computer sector. DisplayPort uses a self-clocking micro-packet-based protocol that allows for a variable number of differential lanes as well as flexible allocation of bandwidth between audio and video, and allows encapsulating multichannel compressed audio formats in the audio stream.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DisplayPort_CEA2010_206-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DisplayPort_CEA2010-206">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        200
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
       <a href="#cite_note-207">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        201
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      DisplayPort ports can be made so that they are compatible with single-link
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_Visual_Interface" title="Digital Visual Interface">
       DVI
      </a>
      and HDMI 1.4.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DP_Interop_208-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DP_Interop-208">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        202
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Compatibility is achieved with
      <a href="/wiki/DisplayPort#Dual-mode" title="DisplayPort">
       DisplayPort Dual-mode
      </a>
      ports, which are marked with the ++DP logo, using attached passive adapters; powered active adapters allow signal conversion to dual-link DVI and analog
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VGA" title="VGA">
       VGA
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DisplayPort_CEA2010_206-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DisplayPort_CEA2010-206">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        200
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DP_Interop_208-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DP_Interop-208">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        202
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      DisplayPort has a royalty rate of $0.20 per unit (from patents licensed by MPEG LA) while HDMI has an
      <a href="#Cost">
       annual fee of $10,000 and a per unit royalty rate of between $0.15 to $0.04
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DisplayPortMPEGLicenseMarch2015_209-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DisplayPortMPEGLicenseMarch2015-209">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        203
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      DisplayPort version 1.2 added the ability to transport multiple audio/video streams, doubled the maximum data rate from 10.8 Gbit/s to 21.6 Gbit/s, increased the "AUX" channel bandwidth from 1 Mbit/s to 720 Mbit/s, added the ability to use multiple color spaces including
      <a href="/wiki/XvYCC" title="XvYCC">
       xvYCC
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/ScRGB" title="ScRGB">
       scRGB
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adobe_RGB_1998" title="Adobe RGB 1998">
       Adobe RGB 1998
      </a>
      , added global time-code for audio synchronisation and the ability to transfer Ethernet, USB 2.0, DPMS, and other types of data over the "AUX" channel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DisplayPort_CEA2010_206-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-DisplayPort_CEA2010-206">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        200
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DevCon2010_210-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DevCon2010-210">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        204
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCMagDisplayPort1.2_211-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PCMagDisplayPort1.2-211">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        205
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      HDMI has a few advantages over DisplayPort, such as ability to carry
      <a href="#CEC">
       Consumer Electronics Control
      </a>
      (CEC) signals, and electrical compatibility with DVI (though practically limited to single-link DVI rates).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCMagDisplayPort1.2_211-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-PCMagDisplayPort1.2-211">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        205
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
       <a href="#cite_note-212">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        206
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
       <a href="#cite_note-213">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        207
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      More importantly, HDMI can sustain full bandwidth for up to 10 meters of cable length, while Displayport can carry full bandwidth for up to 3 meters only which makes it unusable for most home theater projector applications.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
       <a href="#cite_note-214">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        208
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_MHL">
       Relationship with MHL
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=HDMI&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Relationship with MHL">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_High-definition_Link" title="Mobile High-definition Link">
       Mobile High-definition Link
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Mobile High-definition Link (MHL) is an
      <a href="/wiki/Technical_standard" title="Technical standard">
       industry standard
      </a>
      for a mobile audio/video interface for directly connecting mobile phones and other portable
      <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">
       consumer electronics
      </a>
      (CE) devices to
      <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">
       high-definition televisions
      </a>
      (HDTVs) and displays.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLSampling2008_215-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MHLSampling2008-215">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        209
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumSI2009_216-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumSI2009-216">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        210
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumEETimes2010_217-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumEETimes2010-217">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        211
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      MHL is developed by the
      <b>
       MHL Consortium
      </b>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Consortium" title="Consortium">
       consortium
      </a>
      of leading CE and mobile manufacturers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumSI2009_216-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumSI2009-216">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        210
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumEETimes2010_217-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumEETimes2010-217">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        211
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many of the companies behind MHL are also the ones behind HDMI.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumSI2009_216-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumSI2009-216">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        210
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumEETimes2010_217-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumEETimes2010-217">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        211
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      MHL features:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Power is transmitted through the cable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ_218-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ-218">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         212
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Typical cases include the TV charging the mobile device and the mobile device powering an active MHL to HDMI dongle.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ_218-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ-218">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         212
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Uses a single, thin cable to connect the mobile device to the TV compared to HDMI.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ_218-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ-218">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         212
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Typical MHL cables are 1.5m long.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDMI-CEC" title="HDMI-CEC">
        HDMI-CEC
       </a>
       capability.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWC2011_interview_219-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MWC2011_interview-219">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         213
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Video resolution limited to
       <a href="/wiki/1080p" title="1080p">
        1080p
       </a>
       uncompressed 4:2:2 HD video (PacketVideo) or
       <a href="/wiki/720p" title="720p">
        720p
       </a>
       4:4:4 HD video. MHL 2.0 provides for 1080p at 60Hz.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Engadget2012MHL2chips_220-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Engadget2012MHL2chips-220">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         214
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       8 channel (e.g.,
       <a href="/wiki/7.1_surround_sound" title="7.1 surround sound">
        7.1 surround sound
       </a>
       ) uncompressed audio.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ_218-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ-218">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         212
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Allows
       <a href="/wiki/High-bandwidth_Digital_Content_Protection" title="High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection">
        High-bandwidth Digital Content Protection
       </a>
       (HDCP).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ_218-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-MHLConsortiumWebsiteFAQ-218">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         212
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Typical MHL connector is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micro_USB" title="Micro USB">
        micro USB
       </a>
       , a typical connector already found in many mobile devices. The same micro USB connector can be used to charge the device, to establish data communication with a computer and to transfer uncompressed video.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      On January 6, 2015, MHL announced the superMHL specification, the next-generation of MHL technology for CE and mobile devices. superMHL delivers mobile advancements such as higher resolution and frame rates along with 40W of power charging, while broadening MHLs reach in home theater connectivity by supporting 8K video resolution and expanded audio formats. With superMHL, consumers can link their mobile devices, set-top boxes (STBs), Blu-ray Disc players, AVRs, streaming media sticks and other source devices to TVs and displays. The release of a new reversible superMHL connector supports enhanced video formats to deliver lifelike, immersive content between home theater products and displays.
     </p>
     <p>
      Features of superMHL include:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Delivery of up to 8K 120fps video
      </li>
      <li>
       Deep Color support up to 48-bit color depths
      </li>
      <li>
       Wider color gamut to view content the way filmmakers intended
      </li>
      <li>
       High-Dynamic Range (HDR) support to strike the perfect balance of bright spectral highlights along with shadow details
      </li>
      <li>
       Immersive surround sound with support for object audio such as Dolby Atmos, DTS:X, 3D audio, and an audio-only mode
      </li>
      <li>
       Advanced connectivity configurations to link multiple MHL devices together (TV, AVR, Blu-ray player) and control them via one remote
      </li>
      <li>
       Power charging up to 40W
      </li>
      <li>
       Content on multiple displays when connecting a single device
      </li>
      <li>
       Reversible superMHL connector
      </li>
      <li>
       Support for the MHL Alt Mode for the
       <a href="/wiki/USB_Type-C" title="USB Type-C">
        USB Type-C
       </a>
       specification
      </li>
     </ul>

       <li id="cite_note-20">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-20">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation journal">
          Alen Koebel (February 2003).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.widescreenreview.com/" rel="nofollow">
           "DVI and HDMI: Digital A/V Interfaces for A New Age"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           Widescreen Review
          </i>
          (69): 64
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            June 24,
           </span>
           2008
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           When HDCP is added to DVI, the result is often called "DVI+HDCP." When this is used on an HDTV, HD monitor or set-top box, a further standard is usually applied: IEA/CEA-861 (currently 861-B)...the interface is commonly known as DVI-HDTV.
          </q>
         </span>

          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
